Could you please provide me with some experiences that you may have with them to make my decision simpler?","dateCreated":"2013-04-10T16:19:29+0000","answerCount":21,"dateModified":"2013-04-17T15:34:36+0000","keywords":"Text Mining,Natural Language Processing","author":{"@type":"Person","name":"Mohsen Farhadloo","mainEntityOfPage":{"@type":"URL","@id":"https:\/\/www.researchgate.net\/profile\/Mohsen_Farhadloo#profile"}},"acceptedAnswer":{"@type":"Answer","upvoteCount":8,"text":"The choice of tool depends on the specific problem you are dealing in Sentiment Analysis. Except rapidminer, I have used each of them in different scenarios.\n \n I am giving a quick account of them and hope this can assist you in picking the right option for your problem.\n \n StanfordCoreNLP :- If you need part of speech categories, syntactic analysis (phrase structure OR dependency analysis), co-reference or named entities in text. These have been used as potential features by the sentiment analysis research community. \n \n WEKA :- If you already have data with each data point having a feature vector then you can use Weka for clustering your data. If you also have the gold predicted outputs for your data you can build classifiers. Highly configurable and easy to use GUI available\n\n NLTK :- If you know programming in python then NLTK is a smart choice as it includes the functionalists of the above two. Other than this you can easily make use of lexical resources like WordNet often required in sentiment analysis.\n \n GATE :- Useful if you want to develop a pipeline. Language analysis modules for various languages are contributed by developers are available to be used plugged in your pipeline. If you have a new approach you can write a customized module in JAVA and plug into the pipeline and a complete system will be available.","dateCreated":"2013-04-10T20:30:26+0000","author":{"@type":"Person","name":"Sambhav Jain"}}}</script>

               <div class="post-content rich-text-styled" id="rgw8_59d3925e1e1a6"> 
                <h1 class="topic-post-title"> Available tools for text mining, NLP and sentiment analysis. </h1> 
                <div class="topic-post-text">
                  I have recently been involved in the research field of sentiment analysis. Sentiment analysis or opinion mining involves large amount of text mining and natural language processing. By a quick research I found that MATLAB is not a suitable tool for text mining and I was wondering what other tools are out there that are widely used by text miners. I have heard about the following codes, softwares and tools but have a hard time to make a decision: StanfordCoreNLP, weka, GATE, rapid miner and python NLTK. Could you please provide me with some experiences that you may have with them to make my decision simpler? 
                </div> 
               </div>
              </div>
             </div> 
            </div>

                   <div id="rgw42_59d3925e1e1a6" class="post-edit-content comment-body topic-post-text rich-text-styled">
                     The choice of tool depends on the specific problem you are dealing in Sentiment Analysis. Except rapidminer, I have used each of them in different scenarios.
                    <br> 
                    <br> I am giving a quick account of them and hope this can assist you in picking the right option for your problem.
                    <br> 
                    <br> StanfordCoreNLP :- If you need part of speech categories, syntactic analysis (phrase structure OR dependency analysis), co-reference or named entities in text. These have been used as potential features by the sentiment analysis research community. 
                    <br> 
                    <br> WEKA :- If you already have data with each data point having a feature vector then you can use Weka for clustering your data. If you also have the gold predicted outputs for your data you can build classifiers. Highly configurable and easy to use GUI available
                    <br> 
                    <br> NLTK :- If you know programming in python then NLTK is a smart choice as it includes the functionalists of the above two. Other than this you can easily make use of lexical resources like WordNet often required in sentiment analysis.
                    <br> 
                    <br> GATE :- Useful if you want to develop a pipeline. Language analysis modules for various languages are contributed by developers are available to be used plugged in your pipeline. If you have a new approach you can write a customized module in JAVA and plug into the pipeline and a complete system will be available. 
                   </div>
                  </div>
                 </div> 
                </div> 
                <div> 
                 <span class="answer-post-likes">
                  <div id="rgw44_59d3925e1e1a6" class="react-container">

               <div class="actions-secondary rf"> 
               </div> 
               <div class="comment-image"> 
                <a href="profile/Jose_Gomez_Hidalgo"> <img width="30" height="30" src="https://i1.rgstatic.net/ii/profile.image/AS%3A370623210639361%401465374867709_m/Jose_Gomez_Hidalgo.jpg" title="Jose Maria Gomez Hidalgo" alt="Jose Maria Gomez Hidalgo"> </a> 
               </div> 
               <div class="comment-content"> 
                <div class="comment-author"> 
                 <strong><a href="profile/Jose_Gomez_Hidalgo">Jose Maria Gomez Hidalgo</a></strong> · Pragsis 
                </div> 
                <div class="js-content"> 
                 <div id="rgw102_59d3925e1e1a6" class="react-container">
                  <div class="js-backend-rendered" data-reactroot="" data-reactid="1" data-react-checksum="2004787487">
                   <div id="rgw103_59d3925e1e1a6" class="post-edit-content comment-body topic-post-text rich-text-styled">
                     Dear Mohsen
                    <br> 
                    <br> I am a WEKA fan (so my opinions are biased), and I have used it for many text mining projects. I believe it is simple and enough for most text mining projects, including sentiment analysis. In fact, I have recently posted a tutorial in my blog on how to perform sentiment analysis with WEKA, you may be interested on it: 
                    <a href="https://www.researchgate.net/deref/http%3A%2F%2Fjmgomezhidalgo.blogspot.com.es%2F2013%2F06%2Fbaseline-sentiment-analysis-with-weka.html" rel="noopener" target="_blank">http://jmgomezhidalgo.blogspot.com.es/2013/06/baseline-sentiment-analysis-with-weka.html</a>. The source code and the dataset (WEKA-formatted) are available there or at my GitHub repository: 
                    <a href="https://www.researchgate.net/deref/https%3A%2F%2Fgithub.com%2Fjmgomezh%2Ftmweka%2Ftree%2Fmaster%2FOpinionMining" rel="noopener" target="_blank">https://github.com/jmgomezh/tmweka/tree/master/OpinionMining</a>.
                    <br> 
                    <br> As an alternative, you may want to try to employ a lexical-based approach using a sentiment/polarity lexicon like SentiWordNet - you can check a simple example in my blog as well: 
                    <a href="https://www.researchgate.net/deref/http%3A%2F%2Fjmgomezhidalgo.blogspot.com.es%2F2013%2F06%2Fcomparing-baselines-of-keyword-and.html" rel="noopener" target="_blank">http://jmgomezhidalgo.blogspot.com.es/2013/06/comparing-baselines-of-keyword-and.html</a>.
                    <br> 
                    <br> Another alternative is using LingPipe: 
                    <a href="https://www.researchgate.net/deref/http%3A%2F%2Falias-i.com%2Flingpipe%2Fdemos%2Ftutorial%2Fsentiment%2Fread-me.html" rel="noopener" target="_blank">http://alias-i.com/lingpipe/demos/tutorial/sentiment/read-me.html</a>
                    <br> 
                    <br> Hope this helps, and regards
                    <br> 
                    <br> Jose Maria 
                   </div>
                  </div>
                 </div> 
                </div>

Except rapidminer, I have used each of them in different scenarios.\\n \\n I am giving a quick account of them and hope this can assist you in picking the right option for your problem.\\n \\n StanfordCoreNLP :- If you need part of speech categories, syntactic analysis (phrase structure OR dependency analysis), co-reference or named entities in text. These have been used as potential features by the sentiment analysis research community. \\n \\n WEKA :- If you already have data with each data point having a feature vector then you can use Weka for clustering your data. If you also have the gold predicted outputs for your data you can build classifiers. Highly configurable and easy to use GUI available\\n\\n NLTK :- If you know programming in python then NLTK is a smart choice as it includes the functionalists of the above two. Other than this you can easily make use of lexical resources like WordNet often required in sentiment analysis.\\n \\n GATE :- Useful if you want to develop a pipeline. Language analysis modules for various languages are contributed by developers are available to be used plugged in your pipeline. If you have a new approach you can write a customized module in JAVA and plug into the pipeline and a complete system will be
